# Slicer-5.2.2-linux-amd64/Slicer does not launch

**Topic ID**: 31318
**Date**: 2023-08-23
**URL**: https://discourse.slicer.org/t/slicer-5-2-2-linux-amd64-slicer-does-not-launch/31318

---

## Post #1 by @tbillah (2023-08-23 17:45 UTC)

<p>Slicer-5.2.2-linux-amd64/Slicer shows the splash screen but then nothing happens. No logs are printed on the parent terminal either. It remains hanging forever. I am on a CentOS 7 Linux computer. Is there any log we can look into? Please advise.</p>

---

## Post #2 by @pieper (2023-08-23 17:57 UTC)

<p>The initial splash screen is from the launcher which sets variables and then launches real app.  You can use the launcher to start a shell to test in with:<br>
<code>Slicer --launch /bin/bash</code><br>
In that shell you can try running:<br>
<code>strace SlicerApp-real</code><br>
to see what system calls are being made.  Maybe you will see what is happening as the app tries to launch.  You may also try <code>ldd SlicerApp-real</code> to confirm how shared libraries are resolved.</p>

---

<p>Seeing the following ones:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-auto">    libgssapi_krb5.so.2 =&gt; /lib64/libgssapi_krb5.so.2 (0x00007fae63236000)

<p>lead me to think we are facing:</p>

    <h4>
      <a href="https://github.com/Slicer/Slicer/issues/5663" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Crash on Fedora 33 due to OpenSSL/Kerberos incompatibility</a>
    </h4>

    <div class="github-info">
      <div class="date">
        opened <span class="discourse-local-date" data-format="ll" data-date="2021-05-31" data-time="09:00:11" data-timezone="UTC">09:00AM - 31 May 21 UTC</span>

        <a href="https://github.com/renatobellotti" target="_blank" rel="noopener">

  <div class="github-row">
    <p class="github-body-container">3D Slicer crashes with the following error message:

```
Slicer-4.11.20210226<span class="show-more-container"><a href="" rel="noopener" class="show-more">â€¦</a></span><span class="excerpt hidden">-linux-amd64/bin/SlicerApp-real: symbol lookup error: /lib64/libk5crypto.so.3: undefined symbol: EVP_KDF_ctrl, version OPENSSL_1_1_1b
```

## Steps to reproduce

Download the latest binary and run it on Fedora.

## Expected behavior

The program should start.

## Environment
- Slicer version: Slicer-4.11.20210226-linux-amd64
- Operating system: Fedora 33</span></p>
  </div>

## Post #8 by @pieper (2023-08-24 13:12 UTC)

<p>Good catch <a class="mention" href="/u/jcfr">@jcfr</a> <img src="https://emoji.discourse-cdn.com/twitter/+1.png?v=12" title=":+1:" class="emoji" alt=":+1:" loading="lazy" width="20" height="20"></p>
<p><a class="mention" href="/u/tbillah">@tbillah</a> do you have access to the Martinos Center systems?  You can copy <code>/usr/pubsw/packages/slicer/Slicer-5.2.2-linux-amd64</code> from there and it should work to run the <code>slicer522</code> script.  If you donâ€™t have access anyone who does can copy it for you.</p>
<p>Or you could build openssl and krb5 yourself and put them in the directory with Slicer.  Hereâ€™s the contents of the <code>slicer522</code> script:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-auto">#!/usr/bin/env bash

SCRIPT_DIR=$( cd -- "$( dirname -- "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}" )" &amp;&gt; /dev/null &amp;&amp; pwd )

LD_LIBRARY_PATH=${SCRIPT_DIR}/openssl:${SCRIPT_DIR}/krb5/src/lib:${LD_LIBRARY_PATH} ${SCRIPT_DIR}/Slicer $*
</code></pre>

---

## Post #10 by @pieper (2023-08-24 15:12 UTC)

<p>At least on the Martinos system the openssl version was not the correct one, and upgrading the system was not an option so I needed to build both from source.  They werenâ€™t hard to build; just the defaults as I recall.</p>

<p>I have different Slicer versions for incompatible extensions and I lose one or two hours reinstalling everything every time this happens.</p>
<p>Hope you can help <img src="https://emoji.discourse-cdn.com/twitter/slight_smile.png?v=12" title=":slight_smile:" class="emoji" alt=":slight_smile:" loading="lazy" width="20" height="20"></p>

---

## Post #12 by @lassoan (2024-02-20 23:32 UTC)

<p>Slicer is fully portable - all library and data file locations are resolved relative to the install folder. Therefore, moving the whole install folder should not cause any problems. You can verify that portability works fine by installing Slicer into a folder, check if it runs correctly, and then move it to another location, and check if it still works well.</p>
<p>When you use ldd make sure you run it using the launcher (<code>./Slicer --launch ldd ...</code>). Without the launcher setting up rhe environment, none of the shared libraries will be found.</p>

---
